  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c4b5ed9b-0a94-4315-89e9-e63eb8624e3f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText15942174113394555258" style="display:none"><b>A laird trapped between centuries...</b><br /><br />Enchanted by a powerful spell, Highland laird Drustan MacKeltar slumbered for nearly five centuries hidden deep in a cave, until an unlikely savior awakened him. The enticing lass who dressed and spoke like no woman he’d ever known was from his distant future, where crumbled ruins were all that remained of his vanished world. Drustan knew he had to return to his own century if he was to save his people from a terrible fate. And he needed the bewitching woman by his side....<br /><br /><b>A woman changed forever in his arms...</b><br /><br />Gwen Cassidy had come to Scotland to shake up her humdrum life and, just maybe, meet a man. How could she have known that a tumble down a Highland ravine would send her plunging into an underground cavern — to land atop the most devastatingly seductive man she’d ever seen? Or that once he’d kissed her, he wouldn’t let her go? <br /><br />Bound to Drustan by a passion stronger than time, Gwen is swept back to sixteenth-century Scotland, where a treacherous enemy plots against them... and where a warrior with the power to change history will defy time itself for the woman he loves....</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_147627883" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147627883" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147627883?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=romance-romance-romance">romance-romance-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=should-have-been-bad">should-have-been-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147627883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2925439325075288184">Yes, in case you're wondering, I'm even more ashamed than when I gave its predeccesor <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/815150.The_Highlander_s_Touch__Highlander___3_' title='The Highlander's Touch (Highlander, #3) by Karen Marie Moning' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Highlander's Touch</a> three stars. It seems that I'm deteriorating into some obscure form of madness in which time-travelling, historical romance can illicit a four star rating out of me.<br/><br/>They should name a damn charitable foundation after me to help other people suffering from this obscure mental illness.<br/><br/>But it's honestly not my fault. The fault lies with Karen Marie Moning.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345557i/700165.jpg' alt='Evil' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>There it is, folks. The face of pure</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2925439325075288184" style="display:none">Yes, in case you're wondering, I'm even more ashamed than when I gave its predeccesor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/815150.The_Highlander_s_Touch__Highlander___3_" title="The Highlander's Touch (Highlander, #3) by Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">The Highlander's Touch</a> three stars. It seems that I'm deteriorating into some obscure form of madness in which time-travelling, historical romance can illicit a four star rating out of me.<br><br>They should name a damn charitable foundation after me to help other people suffering from this obscure mental illness.<br><br>But it's honestly not my fault. The fault lies with Karen Marie Moning.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345557i/700165.jpg" alt="Evil" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>There it is, folks. The face of pure evil.</i><br><br>She makes these RIDICULOUS books that you should blush at the idea of reading - readable, fun and hilarious. If I deign to pick up a Historical Romance - especially one in which time-travelling is involved - I would spend most of it groaning, rolling my eyes and looking for a wall to bash my head on. <br><br>And yet, here we are. I've read two books in this series now and I have no intention of stopping. I mean, I totally could stop. If I wanted to...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345557i/700166._SX540_.jpg" alt="Addict" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I could stop anytime...</i><br><br>The strongest part of this book is, without a doubt, the characters. They're fantastic. Gwen and Drustan had me in hysterics. I thought this was going to be the usual pushy, chauvinistic male character with sex-pot-in-the-making virgin who admires his studly-studlyness until they have great sex and babies and we forget that they ever had issues. No. This is a story where the pushy, chauvinistic male character gets locked in the privy by the brilliant and stubborn female protagonist until he learns to behave himself. I feel this is a trend that already should have existed in many more romances. Because women have been writing 'romantic' men who're really just giant jackasses for waaaaaaaaaaayyyyyyy too long.<br><br>I absolutely adored this book from start to finish and it's not because I like romances. Or history. Or time-travelling. It's because Karen Marie Moning has me wrapped around her twisted little finger as she kicks my ass with her story-telling ability and writing craft. I'm only glad I wasn't a fan of such books BEFORE I read Moning's, because otherwise she would have ruined Historical Romances as thoroughly for me as she's ruined Urban Fantasy with her Fever Series.<br><br>Simply because she can, the heartless bitch!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2925439325075288184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br><br><br><b> The cover </b> - my oh my can it be more hot?! <a href="http://s1196.photobucket.com/albums/aa412/Chill_Out_Zone/?action=view&amp;current=72866.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> Love the pic, and I'd sure like to meet that model just to see how good a Highlander kiss can be :)))) <br><br><br><b> The story </b> - I loved the whole concept, and it was well written, mixing time travel with druids and magic... Just wow! <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=279453.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> It's about Gwen, an american girl on vacation in Scotland. She is in search of a cherry picker <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=703126.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

So one day, during a field trip, she falls into a cave and stumbles upon a body, a perfectly preserved specimen of human male perfection <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=fansmiley.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> Drustan awakens in this new world, he doesn't know what happened to him, and now must find a way to undo everything and restore the Keltar clan.<br><br><br><b> Drustan </b> - I so loved him <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=378786.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374019i/727907.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> one of the favorite Highlanders I've read &lt;3 He is the head of his clan, and bearer of the druid lore. They have served and protected mankind for centuries, and it is his duty that his line continues, and the druid knowledge be perserved. Unfortunately, he awakens in the future, and finds his home destroyed, meaning that his line was broken and the lore forgotten. That's why he comes up with a plan that could make Gwen hate him forever... <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=fear.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><br><b> Gwen </b> - a great heroine <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=167153.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/361833.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> She's instantly attracted to Drustan (can't blame the girl) and she falls for him in the short time they had before he found his home. She decides to give her virginity to him, and they "do it" in the middle of the stone circle (some druid stuff). They form a bond, he vows love to her, and then attempts to go back in time to undo what has happened to him. BUT, the plan fails (doesn't it always), and Gwen finds herself alone in the past, with Drustan and his family believing her a crazed woman wanting to trap him in marriage XD<br><br><br><b> Overall </b> - This was such a great read, it really got me by surprise! I have to say the author's writing is waaaay waaaay better than the first one, and I'm so glad! I loved the fact that for almost first half of the book Gwen thought Drustan was a madman with his claimes that he's from the past, and almost all the second half Drustan believed Gwen was the crazy one with her claims of being from the future XD This was very well written, I could see that this kind of plotline could be developed in so many ways (bad ones at that), and am so glad this turned out the way it did :)<br><br><br><b> Favorite scenes </b><br>- when Drustan awakens and starts dressing himself, and Gwen notices the million and one knives on him loool<br>- Drustan's first car ride<br>- when they went shopping, him trying on jeans - HOT scene!! <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=fansmiley.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>- he discovers his castle's ruins and is heartbroken <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=468813.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/374889.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>- Gwen's first conversation with the Drustan from the past XD<br>- when they lock him up to have the second conversation <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=355146.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/362691.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26964460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3964563599808037675">Drustan and Gwen's story - I enjoyed this book, it was my first KMM book ever! This is one of KMM's funniest books. I love how Gwen was looking for a cherry picker to rid her of her virginity then when she saw Drustan she thought he looked more like a cherry tree chopper downer than a cherry picker. <br/><br/><br/><br/>The storyline was very good, I love the part toward the end when Drustan remembers then they have a very passionate encounter in the buttery. Gwen was a great heroine, she was intelligent, honorable </span>
  <span id="freeText3964563599808037675" style="display:none">Drustan and Gwen's story - I enjoyed this book, it was my first KMM book ever! This is one of KMM's funniest books. I love how Gwen was looking for a cherry picker to rid her of her virginity then when she saw Drustan she thought he looked more like a cherry tree chopper downer than a cherry picker. <br /><br /><br /><br />The storyline was very good, I love the part toward the end when Drustan remembers then they have a very passionate encounter in the buttery. Gwen was a great heroine, she was intelligent, honorable and smart enough to figure out how to trap Drustan in his own guarderobe. This story was a great set up for the next book, Dark Highlander. Highly recommeded!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3964563599808037675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I also just can't stand the term "make love" or "Love making" and found this book incredibly frustrating and too much instalove. <br/><br/>There were moments I enjoyed, I want to read the next book but overall to cheesy for me. Maybe because of the year it was published? Moving on.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/374703554?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/3024056-karla">Karla</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6283298-kiss-of-the-highlander">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!! </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Karla by: </span>
      Kristen, Kris
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=angst-filled">angst-filled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=awesome-alpha">awesome-alpha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=exciting">exciting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=larger-than-life-character">larger-than-life-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=laugh-out-loud-funny">laugh-out-loud-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=witty">witty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=reunited-lovers">reunited-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sensual">sensual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sizzling-romance">sizzling-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=spunky-heroine">spunky-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer374703554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17466380987965322784"><b>5 Gigantic Stars!!! FANTASTICAL!!</b> It was worth all the anxiety I felt for reading out of order. A few pages in and all that OCD flew out the window!! <br/><i><br/>“If aught must be lost, ‘twill be my honor for yours. If one must be forsaken, ‘twill be my soul for yours. Should death come anon, ‘twill be my life for yours. I am Given.”</i><br/><br/>This book had everything and then some that I look for in a story. A larger than life hero, who is cocky, funny, protective, loving, worships his woman and is SCRUMPTIOUS! Drust</span>
  <span id="freeText17466380987965322784" style="display:none"><b>5 Gigantic Stars!!! FANTASTICAL!!</b> It was worth all the anxiety I felt for reading out of order. A few pages in and all that OCD flew out the window!! <br /><i><br />“If aught must be lost, ‘twill be my honor for yours. If one must be forsaken, ‘twill be my soul for yours. Should death come anon, ‘twill be my life for yours. I am Given.”</i><br /><br />This book had everything and then some that I look for in a story. A larger than life hero, who is cocky, funny, protective, loving, worships his woman and is SCRUMPTIOUS! Drustan MacKeltar...<b>RAWRRRRRR!!!</b> A heroine who stands on her own will, she's mouthy, pushy, smart, challenges her man and loves him beyond reason! Gwen Cassidy...<b>AMAZING</b>!! A story that captivates, charms, tugs at the heart! Passion, desire and love that is breathtaking and heart-pounding...<b>YES!!!</b> Secondary characters that play a huge role in the plot and are so intriguing, you hope that you get more of them, in future books or stories of their own. <br /><br />I was overwhelmed with emotion while reading this book, but the last few pages made my eyes so wet, I could barely read to the end. I damn near passed out with Kip clutched in my hands! When I could finally breathe, I began to smile and I still can't get that shit-ass grin off my face. <br /><br />Thank you to my dear friend Kristen, who convinced me to step out of the box and read out of order. It was no easy task for her to do, but I trust her and knew she wouldn't steer me wrong. Not to mention all of my other GR friends who agreed with her and encouraged me to go for it. You were all right, I didn't miss a thing. This books starts what is a mini-series within a series. It was everything you all said it would be and more. <b>Thank you!!</b><br /><br />Finally to Kris, who told me about her love for this series a while back. Why I didn't listen to you is beyond me. It's always been in the back of my mind and your profile pic was a daily reminder. You know me better than I know myself.<br /><br /><b>Dark Highlander here I come!!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17466380987965322784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1199270119505819069" style="display:none"><b>KISS OF A HIGHLANDER</b><br><br><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/58734075@N06/5481657934/" title="kilt by Sam aka S2, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345238i/699944.jpg" width="260" height="330" alt="kilt" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Okay, now I have your attention I would like to say - hasnt the model on the cover of this book have the most kissable lips you have ever seen? What I would give to have them babies roaming my body...oh my - im sweating here....<br><br><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/58734075@N06/5481663548/" title="414TZBFgbWL__SS500_ by Sam aka S2, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345238i/699945.jpg" width="240" height="240" alt="414TZBFgbWL__SS500_" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>LMAO...Okay, now the review -<br><br>Well, well, well looky what I stumbled across here – HUNKY HIGHLANDERS – my lordy lord, this book was more than I ever perceived it was going to be. If it wasn’t for my fabulous GR friend, Nissie, I would not have taken the plunge to read this so soon.<br><br>Okay so about the story – This is my first time travelling book, and initially my thoughts on time travel are simply – meh – but when introduced to Drustan MacKeltar who is from the 16th century, I melted. This scot is a drop dead, kilt wearing hunk of spunk AND to make it all that much sweeter *drool drips from mouth* he goes completely commando! On the theory that if it isn’t constricted then it will continue to grow (hmm...an interesting theory I would love to test on any willing hunky participants)....Any who, gypsy’s cast a nasty ass spell on him to sleep for all eternity, only able to be awaked by sun and blood. He is placed in a cave where he sleeps for 500 years. That is until our minx of a heroine klutzily stumbles across his hidey hole and BAM SLAM THANKYOU MAM – the story get hot.<br><br><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/58734075@N06/5481654768/" title="Scottish_man_skirt_0 by Sam aka S2, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345238i/699946.jpg" width="400" height="296" alt="Scottish_man_skirt_0" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Gwen is on vacation to Scotland, touring with a bunch of pensioners (completely by accident) – I found this funny because the same thing happens to me when I was 15. Went on a tour in Canada and It turned out to be a tour for pensioners. I actually ended up having a blast and came to respect the elderly much more. Her main goal while in Scotland – TO FIND A CHERRY PICKER...LMAO!!!! When Gwen falls into Drustens cave she awakens the hunk of spunk and instantly their passion for one another is palpable. <br><br>Gwen sets out to help Drusten get back to his own time (she's not really aware of it, but she’s along for the ride), he needs to get back to his time to save his clan. Unfortunately he sends them back too far into time thus erasing himself. Gwen is then left to convince the 16th century Drusten that they are meant to be together.<br><br><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/58734075@N06/5481648368/" title="boots by Sam aka S2, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345238i/699947.jpg" width="246" height="366" alt="boots" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was a wild ride, and I am so glad that I read it. I cannot wait to get my greedy little mitts on the next one, which if I gather correctly is about Drustens twin and equally as sexy brother. <br><br>Happy reading ladies.<br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616956233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18161879063338668723">Once upon a time 'a girl who was hiking in the foothills of Scotland found an enchanted highlader sleeping in a cave above Loch Ness'. A bit clumsy as she was, she lost her balance and landed on top of him waking him up. The sleeping beauty, Drustan, had been slept for 500 years and he was a bit lost when he woke up in 21st century, but Gwen helped him found his way.<br/><br/>This was a great love story!<br/><br/>I had a goofy smile while I was reading it from the beginning until the end. The story is basically div</span>
  <span id="freeText18161879063338668723" style="display:none">Once upon a time 'a girl who was hiking in the foothills of Scotland found an enchanted highlader sleeping in a cave above Loch Ness'. A bit clumsy as she was, she lost her balance and landed on top of him waking him up. The sleeping beauty, Drustan, had been slept for 500 years and he was a bit lost when he woke up in 21st century, but Gwen helped him found his way.<br /><br />This was a great love story!<br /><br />I had a goofy smile while I was reading it from the beginning until the end. The story is basically divided into two parts.<br />-The first part is taking place in the 21st century when Drustan wakes up and Gwen thinks he is completely crazy<br />-The second part is taking place in the 16th century when Gwen travels back in time, Drustan does not remember her and he thinks she is completely crazy.<br /><br />I honestly wished I had read this book and the ones that follow before the Fever series by Moning. Apparently as I realised Drustan is Christian's uncle. Christian is the druid who is helping Mac and in Fever we meet again Drustan and his brother Dugeous.<br /><br />Finally, I know that what I am about to say will sound very boring but doesn't the guy in the bookcover has the most kissable lips you have ever seen? </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2432774599?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2432774599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1566276613470310132"><b> 3 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b>I struggled at times with this one tbh. I love the time travel idea of it, but it just fell a little flat for me. I felt like there was way too much inner dialogue going on (especially in the first half) and not enough actual interactions. The connection between the h and H felt mostly sexual, and I didn't get the progression of feelings to love. The ending also was a huge bummer. We get all this struggle for them and then an ending that didn't even feel complete! Oh wel</span>
  <span id="freeText1566276613470310132" style="display:none"><b> 3 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b>I struggled at times with this one tbh. I love the time travel idea of it, but it just fell a little flat for me. I felt like there was way too much inner dialogue going on (especially in the first half) and not enough actual interactions. The connection between the h and H felt mostly sexual, and I didn't get the progression of feelings to love. The ending also was a huge bummer. We get all this struggle for them and then an ending that didn't even feel complete! Oh well. I did enjoy the characters themselves, and I also enjoyed their banter and the side characters. I'm going to go with a middle of the road 3 Stars, because while I didn't love it I didn't hate it either.<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Gwen and Drustan's story. Gwen is tired of her life and is on a vacation in Scotland when she finds herself falling in a hole and landing on top of a half naked, hot man. After being in what seems to be a coma or deep sleep, Gwen somehow awakens him. Drustan is instantly confused by his surroundings and shocks Gwen when he declares that he is from the 16th century and somehow had been enchanted. Gwen tries to help him because she thinks he's mentally ill, but with their strong attraction and some undeniable magic she can no longer deny that he is speaking the truth. Gwen somehow ends up catapulted back into Drustan's time, and she must warn the past Drustan and his family of the upcoming danger. There are some funny moments, some sexy times, and some sweet moments...and they get a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between focusing mainly on Gwen and Drustan in 3rd person narrative. It did have some parts that focused on side characters as well.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Not the best. It felt slow at times. I skimmed some of the decor descriptions, (seemingly) repetitive inner dialogue, and sex scenes. I don't think I missed much by doing so either.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> Kind of. They don't have much basis to their relationship (other than lust) when they start confessing (at least in their inner dialogue) stronger feelings IMO.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 4 stars. Drustan. I liked him. He was sweet, alpha, and loyal.<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 4 stars. Gwen. I liked her. She was smart, sassy, and brave.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Both of them push away and also pursue the relationship at times.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Good. They have some good tension, chemistry, and scenes. I skimmed some scenes tbh because they did feel like a little bit too much at times.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ When they are reunited, the H is engaged and about to marry OW and this causes some drama for the couple (he's never met this OW). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated a few different times (at least physically), but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The h is a virgin, it is implied the H has had many other partners before h (off page), loss of parents (off page), and unexpected pregnancy (on page)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had an abrupt ending with not nearly enough closure for me! I wanted to know how they fared and how they created their future! It seems as though we'll see them in later books, but I am frustrated I didn't even get a glimpse into their HEA. I would call this a HFN ending just because of my so many unanswered questions, but others might be fine in calling it a HEA <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They're magically bound/married (no ceremony) and she is pregnant <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a few physical separations between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a HEA ending (see above) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36770112?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=celtic-mythology">celtic-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=scottish">scottish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36770112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11624315867264532944">This was a delightful book. Heartwarming and hilarious in turns, it kept my interest. I really enjoy the fact that KMM's heroines tend to be very intelligent and capable. It's nice to see that in romances. I don't see why a heroine can't be smarter than the hero or more accomplished. I'm glad that KMM doesn't adhere to that formula in her novels. Her heroines tend to be on the physically perfect side, but they are so nice, it doesn't annoy me. Drustan was delicious and he was a nice guy too. He </span>
  <span id="freeText11624315867264532944" style="display:none">This was a delightful book. Heartwarming and hilarious in turns, it kept my interest. I really enjoy the fact that KMM's heroines tend to be very intelligent and capable. It's nice to see that in romances. I don't see why a heroine can't be smarter than the hero or more accomplished. I'm glad that KMM doesn't adhere to that formula in her novels. Her heroines tend to be on the physically perfect side, but they are so nice, it doesn't annoy me. Drustan was delicious and he was a nice guy too. He was yearning for a woman to love and accept him. Aww! The scene where Gwen says she loves him just melted my heart because it meant so much to Drustan. I love elements of Scotland and the historical aspects. The druid lore is interesting, and the physics aspect, mind-boggling. <br /><br />This book is steamy and sexy, but the love relationship is always at the forefront. I really loved the tender moments between Drustan and Gwen, and also between his father Silvan and his housekeeper, Nell. <br /><br />I have never been much of a time travel fan, but I really do like what KMM does with the genre. I like that she has plausible science and mixes the Druid lore with physics and mathematics so that you read this book and can definitely believe that Druid magic is just science in a different framework of understanding.<br /><br />The part that annoyed me was the priest's mother, Besseta. She was totally clueless about faith and fate. If only she had listened to her son and trusted that God would take care of him. But if she had done that, would Gwen and Drustan ever have met? Too much to ponder.<br /><br />At any rate, I'm glad I got to read this novel, for the hours of entertainment it gave me. It also gave me some things to think about, such as meddling with fate and how the search for knowledge should never overstep the boundaries of ethics.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11624315867264532944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2327143648501091815">I loved everything about this book, starting with the yummy cover! Oh boy, I could stare at Nathan Kamp's lips for a lifetime!... ;)<br/><br/>Now, focusing on the story itself... Once again, KMM gave us a more-than-wonderful hero (Drustan MacKeltar) but, this time, she gave us an amazing heroine (Gwen Cassidy) who, I admit, I loved better than the hero. And that's something, because I adored Drustan! Gwen was intelligent, funny, feisty and determined; Drustan didn't really stand a chance with her. When sh</span>
  <span id="freeText2327143648501091815" style="display:none">I loved everything about this book, starting with the yummy cover! Oh boy, I could stare at Nathan Kamp's lips for a lifetime!... ;)<br /><br />Now, focusing on the story itself... Once again, KMM gave us a more-than-wonderful hero (Drustan MacKeltar) but, this time, she gave us an amazing heroine (Gwen Cassidy) who, I admit, I loved better than the hero. And that's something, because I adored Drustan! Gwen was intelligent, funny, feisty and determined; Drustan didn't really stand a chance with her. When she locked him in the garderobe to force him into "seeing reason", I did a little happy dance - only in my mind, of course...<br /><br />While I was reading the book, I kept wondering how KMM would solve the "changing the past" issue. I mean, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[once Gwen suceeded in preventing Drustan's enchantment in the 16th century, he wouldn't be in the cave for her to find in the 21st century, they wouldn't fall in love, and so on...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Aaargh, my mind went a little crazy over this, until I reached KMM's "resolution". Good and logical but, like Gwen said when Drustan explained what had happened, "this hurts my head." (LOL)<br /><br />I was planning on taking a break from the series after this book, but I just can't - not after having read Silvan's letter at the end! Thankfully, I'm late to the Highlander party and Dageus's book has already been released, so I don't have to wait. :)<br /></span>

Yay for me! I'm back in the game :D<br><a href="http://s1135.photobucket.com/user/Enhya77/media/SmangItBodyRoll_zps7563e3b2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>I've said this many times that I am not big on Historical romance reads. So it's no surprise that Highlanders for the most part are not my cup of tea. Although there have been some "Gems" in my past. Though I do not follow this series (I've only read this one &amp; book 6) &amp; love both, I would recommend this series based on the fact that I am a fan of Ms. Moning's Fever series, which was born from this series. I do plan to work my way through this series eventually, now that I have these 2 books under my belt.<br><br>I love this book for 2 reasons... Drustan (H) &amp; the story. What more could you ask for? I would say that I do love Gwen as well. I feel her &amp; Drustan are perfectly matched. Their coupling, how it begins to where it leads, was beyond entertaining, heartfelt, &amp; frustratingly erotic.<br><br>I would definitely recommend you read this book. It has everything on it's pages.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16766247526443239762">Well, I didn't hate it. I know that doesn't sound like high praise, but I H A T E time travel books. They get so caught up in their own complications that it's near impossible to disregard the implications. <br/><br/>But this book honestly did it a bit better than most, though that wasn't the highlight. The story just didn't take itself that seriously.   <span id="freeText16766247526443239762" style="display:none">Well, I didn't hate it. I know that doesn't sound like high praise, but I H A T E time travel books. They get so caught up in their own complications that it's near impossible to disregard the implications. <br /><br />But this book honestly did it a bit better than most, though that wasn't the highlight. The story just didn't take itself that seriously. It was fun and sexy, a welcome diversion. <br /><br />It's still only a 2-2.5 because I felt the focus on the heroine's virginity to be a snooze fest, and I did quite a lot of skimming because some of that background was just not why I was reading this. <br /><br />But all in all, I checked off a challenge book and I can now safely say...not for me for this series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3251502558825722428"><b>3.5 Stars rounded up to 4stars. </b><br/><br/>It was a good read. Based on the plots and writing it was definitely good and five stars worthy, but... I didn’t like some of the things. I can’t explain those BUTS without spoiling everything so better not to say anything. But one thing I can say is that constantly talking about a 25 years old heroine's virginity is definitely not cool. Every time the author mentioned something about heroine’s virginity, I consider to mark it DNF, "I am not reading an HP... Am I?</span>
  <span id="freeText3251502558825722428" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars rounded up to 4stars. </b><br /><br />It was a good read. Based on the plots and writing it was definitely good and five stars worthy, but... I didn’t like some of the things. I can’t explain those BUTS without spoiling everything so better not to say anything. But one thing I can say is that constantly talking about a 25 years old heroine's virginity is definitely not cool. Every time the author mentioned something about heroine’s virginity, I consider to mark it DNF, "I am not reading an HP... Am I? Nay." A good plot kept me alive. <br /><br />The heroine was ok. She was strong but her thinking about the virginity and picking up a cheery picker monologue was irritating. <br /><br />The book was safe. I have some issues with the hero but he was honorable and celibate for some time. It was a time travel romance. And I liked the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the heroine didn’t travel back to past to live with him, here the hero come to the heroine to live in present time. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>
  <blockquote>“If aught must be lost, ‘twill be my honor for yours. If one must be forsaken, ‘twill be my soul for yours. Should death come anon, ‘twill be my life for yours. I am Given.” </blockquote>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14241916928937161731">I'm not going to write a lengthy review here as this book is years old and there are already so many reviews but I will say that it's a highly enjoyable Highlander romance with some supernatural time travel elements mixed in and plenty of humour as well as a well-planned and surprisingly complex plot.<br/><br/>Drustan is a wonderful hero and I very much enjoyed seeing him waking in the 21st century after sleeping for hundreds of years and experiencing cars and lighters and such like. The time travel eleme</span>
  <span id="freeText14241916928937161731" style="display:none">I'm not going to write a lengthy review here as this book is years old and there are already so many reviews but I will say that it's a highly enjoyable Highlander romance with some supernatural time travel elements mixed in and plenty of humour as well as a well-planned and surprisingly complex plot.<br /><br />Drustan is a wonderful hero and I very much enjoyed seeing him waking in the 21st century after sleeping for hundreds of years and experiencing cars and lighters and such like. The time travel elements were enmeshed beautifully and Gwen is a wonderfully, determined kickass heroine with a real backbone.<br /><br />Fantastic stuff!<br /><br />4 stars</span>

    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128861455?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog) by: </span>
      ANGELA
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-karen-marie-moning">author-karen-marie-moning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers">keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=drinks-on-me">drinks-on-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=king-of-the-harem">king-of-the-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=my-hottie-harem">my-hottie-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=the-hymen-club">the-hymen-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128861455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4818798337139695687"><b>Posted on<a href='http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/02/review-kiss-of-highlander-by-karen.html' rel='nofollow noopener'></a> Under the Covers</b><br/><br/>Twenty-five year old Gwen Cassidy is on a mission: To find her cherry picker. <br/><br/>On an impulsive trip to Scotland to find said cherry picker, Gwen encounters a “cherry three chopper-downer” in the form a hulking Highlander who is stubborn as a mule and from the 14th century. Lovely. <br/><br/>After a little mishap retrieving her pack, Gwen takes a tumble and lands upon Drustan MacKeltar, straddling the slumbering Highland laird who has been enchanted by a powerful spell five centuri</span>
  <span id="freeText4818798337139695687" style="display:none"><b>Posted on<a href="http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/02/review-kiss-of-highlander-by-karen.html" rel="nofollow noopener"></a> Under the Covers</b><br /><br />Twenty-five year old Gwen Cassidy is on a mission: To find her cherry picker. <br /><br />On an impulsive trip to Scotland to find said cherry picker, Gwen encounters a “cherry three chopper-downer” in the form a hulking Highlander who is stubborn as a mule and from the 14th century. Lovely. <br /><br />After a little mishap retrieving her pack, Gwen takes a tumble and lands upon Drustan MacKeltar, straddling the slumbering Highland laird who has been enchanted by a powerful spell five centuries ago. With sunlight and her blood, Gwen awakens Drustan only to find that he still believes he is in his century. With a vow to help this confused man, Gwen follows Drustan to the place where his castle once stood...only to find it gone. Using Drustan’s Druid powers and stones, he goes back in time, taking Gwen along with him. But when he miscalculates, they find themselves in a time further back before he was enchanted. <br /><br />While I liked the beginning of the book, it wasn’t until the dressing room scene that things started rolling for me. It was in this pivotal moment that I came to love Drustan and Gwen together:<br /><br /><i>“What have you stuffed in your pants, MacKelter?” she demanded.<br />“Nothing that wasn’t God-given,” he replied stiffly.<br />Gwen stared. “There’s no way that’s part of you. You must have gotten a sock or something stuck. Oh, my.” </i><br /><br />Karen Marie Moning incorporates witty dialogue with a sensual miasma of words that any romance reader can appreciate. She may be popular with her urban fantasy books, but I don’t know if they could compare to the raw, erotic nature of her Highlander books. She does romance very, very well. And this book is no exception!<br /><br />Countless times Moning pulls something that alters her characters lives so much that when you finally reach the end, their happy ending is definitely worth the wait. Gwen and Drustan fall in love twice in this book and each time was better than the last. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4818798337139695687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6283298-kiss-of-the-highlander">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wendy by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3024056-karla">Karla</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4485620-wendy?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4485620-wendy?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4485620-wendy?shelf=hot-highlanders">hot-highlanders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4485620-wendy?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4485620-wendy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer376354283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6265674885795835796">Durstan, a hot higlander that's as alpha as they come and loves unconditionally, meets his match with his heroine Gwen. She's smart and pushes all his buttons, both good and bad. <br/><br/>The story is well paced and has a touch of pnr element and time travel which I enjoyed. I also adored the supporting characters in this and found that they played a major part in balancing this great little love story.<br/><br/>This is a romantic and "feel good" read, that had me laughing out loud. It's a winner!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

Wow, I'm kind of speechless.<br/><br/>Druids, time-travel, highlanders and hot, hot romance. This book has it all and that ending left me swooning.</span>

<div id="review_723594109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/723594109" />
    <a title="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good"><img alt="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389962215p2/16734001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723594109?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" href="/user/show/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good">Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723594109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4643082551220646550"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380437205ra/884116.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>A sort of modern, lame, gender reversed, Sottish version of sleeping beauty. I apologise for the length of this <s>rant</s> review, but I have augmented it with pictures, and lyrics from the eighties.</i><br/><br/>WOW! So I just read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/476543.The_Darkest_Night__Lords_of_the_Underworld___1_' title='The Darkest Night (Lords of the Underworld, #1) by Gena Showalter' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Darkest Night</a> and you may have read in my review how peeved I was at the stupid obsessive love between the virginal girl with no personality called <s>Bella Swan, Anastasia Steel,</s> Ashlyn and her hunk of brooding man meat. Well this book was basically EXACTLY THE EFFING SAME! But it was</span>
  <span id="freeText4643082551220646550" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380437205ra/884116.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>A sort of modern, lame, gender reversed, Sottish version of sleeping beauty. I apologise for the length of this <s>rant</s> review, but I have augmented it with pictures, and lyrics from the eighties.</i><br><br>WOW! So I just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/476543.The_Darkest_Night__Lords_of_the_Underworld___1_" title="The Darkest Night (Lords of the Underworld, #1) by Gena Showalter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkest Night</a> and you may have read in my review how peeved I was at the stupid obsessive love between the virginal girl with no personality called <s>Bella Swan, Anastasia Steel,</s> Ashlyn and her hunk of brooding man meat. Well this book was basically EXACTLY THE EFFING SAME! But it was far more lighthearted and <b>I am <i>HOPING</i> that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/48206.Karen_Marie_Moning" title="Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen Marie Moning</a> wrote this book as a satire. If so then she is a comedy genius!</b><br><br>Basically the romance in this novel was so sugary I wasn't sure whether I should laugh or vomit. I just did not understand how the same author who created JZB and Mac could come up with such total saps as Drustan and Gwen. While reading it I felt like Bruce being forced to eat <i>that</i> cake:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380437205ra/884117.gif" width="400" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It was all just way too much for me. <br><br><br>This book is about a time travelling Scottish laird. Sorta. Maybe being from Scotland made it a bit too cringe for me; but when reading time travel I want something more interesting than angsty characters pining for each other. <br><br>The first thing, of many, that bugged me was:<br><br><u>
  <b>Gwen's vapid personality:</b>
</u> <br><br>You know, Gwen is supposed to be a scientist, she has just traveled back in time, but her mind is blissfully empty; she has gone back to 'the age of discovery' but she has no desire to discuss the advances we have discovered since then with them! SHE SIMPLY HAS NO CURIOSITY. UGH. GIVE THEM SOME PENICILLIN. TELL THEM ABOUT EMILY PANKHURST. IMAGINE ALL THE POSSIBILITIES.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/413718.gif" width="400" height="122" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Hermoine can't stand Gwen.</i><br><br>If Gwen is the girl who is going back 500 years with the opportunity to show how far we have advanced then I AM EMBARRASSED AND FURIOUS WITH FATE because, although she is slightly more cocky than was expected from women back then; there is little else aught different with her. <u>She wants a man. She wants babies. She is not interested in pursuing her career. Most of the time it felt like she actively switched off her brain.</u> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298509ra/684822.gif" width="340" height="328" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Even Clint is disgusted.</i><br><br>To be honest I think Moning is being harsh on 15th century woman, I am sure that although they lived in a much more chauvinistic environment, I doubt they were all misogynists or dumb blow up dolls. This is the era that gave us Joan of Arc for gods sake (give or take a hundred years and lets overlook her horrid death please).<br><br>But she is insinuating that an insipid virgin like Gwen would go back in time and simply take the men by storm with her feisty modern ways. Like WOW she knows who Isaac Newton is; she must be strong and smart... but <i>please</i> don't talk about physics in the morning because it hurts her head and she is desperately trying to daydream of new ways to ensnare a man using her body. <br><br><u>
  <b>Gwen's lack of 'experience':</b>
</u><br><br><i>"Her virginity was hardly presented in the best light when she kept snarling at every man she met."</i><br><br>Gwen is, of course, gagging to be rid of her virginity, which is strange as she is in her mid-twenties and hasn't found an opportunity so far. Apparently because she hasn't met a guy she is attracted to (then why plan a thousand dollar trip just to jump on some stranger??). <br><br>Her desperation is offensive and pathetic in equal measure. I have friends who are virgins and they are so by choice...obviously I don't judge them, because they own their own choices. But the way Gwen acts is like a teenager who thinks her virginity is an embarrassing disease.<br> <br>In fact the whole reason she went to Scotland was to 'find her cherry picker', however she accidentally booked herself onto a geriatric bus tour <i>(oh how silly, but honestly can you expect a woman to curl her hair, apply lipstick, and work a computer?!)</i>. Therefore she only met a man when she fell through a hole in the ground and landed on <s>sleeping beauty</s> Drustan. <br><br><i>
  <b>"If he treated her to a few more of those cocky strokes, she might have her first real orgasm without even sacrificing her cherry."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380437205ra/884118.gif" width="400" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ummmm...what?</i><br><br>I beg your pardon? Did I hear you right, Gwen? You are a beautiful, intelligent, adventurous woman in your mid-twenties and not only are you a virgin, but you haven't even had an orgasm? It doesn't necessarily require a man honey... although I am beginning to think that, in your case, changing a light bulb would require a man. <br><br><br><u>
  <b>The sex scenes: (made me want to gag)</b>
</u><br><br>Ok so my rant about the sex scenes shall be quite short, unlike Drustans 'schmenis', which is apparently so large it cant fit inside of modern jeans. Something to do with wearing kilts all the time. (Here is a very quick tangent; why does Moning think people in the fifteenth century were smaller than now??? Drustan mentions how he draws attention because of his height and calls us 21st century peeps <i>'wee folks, the lot of you.'</i> Which is strange because it's not the case; people were much smaller five hundred years ago.)<br><br>So anyhow the sex:<br><br><i>""Lass show me your breasts. Be quit of this thing, lest I tear it to shreds in my haste""</i><br><br>Well obviously this is Moning releasing her inner comedian again, because it certainly made me LOL. But I am still not at all sure what the attraction is with these neanderthal, over possessive, sappy and spoiled males???<br><br><u>Anyway the dialogue during sex was something else:</u><br><i>""Gwen? Do you want me?"<br>"God, yes!"<br>"Did you want me in the blue trews? Did you want me then too?"<br>"Yes."<br>"Do you feel the heat when I touch you? Does it hit you like a thunderbolt?"<br>"Yes.""</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437205i/884119.jpg" width="375" height="301" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Remember that song by Meatloaf, <i>'Took the words right out of my mouth'</i>? <br> <i>[Boy:] On a hot summer night,<br>would you offer your throat to the wolf with the red roses?<br>[Girl:] Will he offer me his mouth?<br>[Boy:] Yes.<br>[Girl:] Will he offer me his teeth?<br>[Boy:] Yes.<br>[Girl:] Will he offer me his jaws?<br>[Boy:] Yes.<br>[Girl:] Will he offer me his hunger?<br>[Boy:] Yes.<br>[Girl:] Again, will he offer me his hunger?<br>[Boy:] Yes!<br>[Girl:]And will he starve without me?<br>[Boy:] Yes!<br>[Girl:] And does he love me?<br>[Boy:] Yes.<br>[Girl:] Yes.<br>[Boy:] On a hot summer night,<br>would you offer your throat to the wolf with the red roses?<br>[Girl:] Yes.<br>[Boy:] I bet you say that to all the boys.</i>"<br><br>Well the dirty talk in the book was a lot less cool than that dialogue, but equally cheesy. <br><br><br><br><i>"He was the last MacKeltar left to sire sons. He glanced speculatively at Gwen."</i><br><br>Most ladies would find this creepy, but for Gwen it set her ovaries on fire with possessive and obsessive lust.<br><br><u>
  <b>SO FINALLY! My last peeve was with Gwens desire to be a wife and get knocked up:</b>
</u><br><br>I will keep this snappy, because I don't really need to explain that I have no problem with procreation or woman wanting babies, I just think there is more out there. <br><br>I would enjoy a book about a happily married mother of five, in her forties, battling it out against vampires or a teenage mum showing that she can can kick zombie ass and read the Gruffolo to her baby! BUT I am not interested in reading about Gwen disregarding her education and the choices given to her, so she can roll into bed with a caveman and happily live out her life like a good little wifey. That is boring.<br><br>If getting knocked up is the thing Gwen is most excited about, after discovering time travel, then I don't like her. This is Gwen's conversation with her ovaries seconds after falling on to Drustan in the cave: <br><br><b>
  <i>"Aw, kiss him, Gwen, clamored a hundred perky eggs. Shut up, she rebuked. We don't even know him, and until moments ago we though he was dead. That's no way to start a relationship. Who's asking for a relationship? Kisskisskiss! her babies-in-waiting insisted."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380437205ra/884120.gif" width="400" height="195" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>"...Drustan was bending over her, gazing down with so much love in his eyes that she gasped and began to cry."</i> <br><br>THE END</span>
  <a data-text-id="4643082551220646550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17926136558243648779" style="display:none">Wow! This is my first book in this series because I heard they were standalones. <span id="freeTextContainer11268626084269058448">Heavy sigh….wipes tears away from face….wow!<br/><br/>I am at a loss for words to describe how much I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112754.Kiss_of_the_Highlander__Highlander___4_' title='Kiss of the Highlander (Highlander, #4) by Karen Marie Moning' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kiss of the Highlander</a>. I was captivated from the first page and I literally did not put the book down until I finished it. Ms. Moning, I want my very own Highlander!<br/><br/>The story was beautiful. It was hot, steamy, romantic, and magical. <br/><br/>Our heroine Gwen, was on a bus tour of Scotland. She decides to go for a hike.   <span id="freeText11268626084269058448" style="display:none">Heavy sigh….wipes tears away from face….wow!<br /><br />I am at a loss for words to describe how much I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112754.Kiss_of_the_Highlander__Highlander___4_" title="Kiss of the Highlander (Highlander, #4) by Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiss of the Highlander</a>. I was captivated from the first page and I literally did not put the book down until I finished it. Ms. Moning, I want my very own Highlander!<br /><br />The story was beautiful. It was hot, steamy, romantic, and magical. <br /><br />Our heroine Gwen, was on a bus tour of Scotland. She decides to go for a hike. Her bag falls and as she goes to retrieve it, she also falls and lands on top of an enchanted Highlander. 500 year old curse broken, he awakens to find Gwen in a compromising position on top of him. What a great introduction to our Highlander Drustan MacKeltar. (For those of you that have read the Fever series, yes, he is a MacKeltar).<br /><br />So there you have it, a 21st century girl meets 16th century Scot. At first, you sympathize with Drustan. Everything is new and strange to him. But he is endearing, he is stubborn, he is handsome and a mathematical genius. He is strangely attired. He carries a lot of weapons. He is strangely attracted to Gwen. Gwen is a very likeable heroine. She is strong, smart, adaptable, and beautiful. Oh, did I mention that she was a virgin? <br /><br />There is also a time travel aspect to this story. Gwen is sent back in time where she needs to change a series of events that cause Drustan to be cursed. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112754.Kiss_of_the_Highlander__Highlander___4_" title="Kiss of the Highlander (Highlander, #4) by Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiss of the Highlander</a> is one of those books that brought out a whole range of emotions in me....I laughed, I cried, I sighed...<br />I ran to the library to get the next book....</span>
  <a data-text-id="11268626084269058448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11983682738147306529" style="display:none">O.k, O.k, fine, I'll admit it. <span id="freeTextContainer12903523049292280835"><b> 5+ stars I Loved it!</b><br/><br/>I can't thank Kristen & Karla enough for encouraging me to read this. I have this thing about reading books in order and can't skip any, but they assured me that it was ok, and that I didn't need to read the first 3 in the series and that I could start with this one. Adding to my phobia of book skipping, the synopsis also had me worried as I am fairly new to HR and have never really liked the thought of time travel stories. I was really apprehensive about going ahead and rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12903523049292280835" style="display:none"><b> 5+ stars I Loved it!</b><br /><br />I can't thank Kristen &amp; Karla enough for encouraging me to read this. I have this thing about reading books in order and can't skip any, but they assured me that it was ok, and that I didn't need to read the first 3 in the series and that I could start with this one. Adding to my phobia of book skipping, the synopsis also had me worried as I am fairly new to HR and have never really liked the thought of time travel stories. I was really apprehensive about going ahead and reading it but their status updates and reviews won me over and I couldn't resist anymore!<br /><br />Gwen was great but Drustan was phenomenal and had me drooling throughout most of the book. There were a couple of fairly steamy sex scenes later on, but the sexual tension from beginning to end was amazing. KMM's remarkable ability to tell a story made this special and the ending was exceptional and very emotional and had me reaching for the box of tissues.<br /><br />I would happily recommend this to anyone who loves a good romance. <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_16387451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16387451" />
    <a title="Eastofoz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/939365-eastofoz"><img alt="Eastofoz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203907098p2/939365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16387451?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eastofoz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eastofoz" href="/user/show/939365-eastofoz">Eastofoz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">KMM fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/939365-eastofoz?shelf=highlander">highlander</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/939365-eastofoz?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16387451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15760930200627864602">This is a strange series for me. I keep thinking it’s going to get a lot better and it just gets modestly better or considerably worse. Luckily this one falls under the modestly better category. <br/><br/>Here we have the story of Drustan and Gwen. Drustan is a Highlander Druid living way back when while Gwen lives in modern times. In a weird and wacky moment she finds herself in a very interesting “position” the first time she meets Drustan. He finds himself thrown into the 20th century trying to get a g</span>
  <span id="freeText15760930200627864602" style="display:none">This is a strange series for me. I keep thinking it’s going to get a lot better and it just gets modestly better or considerably worse. Luckily this one falls under the modestly better category. <br /><br />Here we have the story of Drustan and Gwen. Drustan is a Highlander Druid living way back when while Gwen lives in modern times. In a weird and wacky moment she finds herself in a very interesting “position” the first time she meets Drustan. He finds himself thrown into the 20th century trying to get a grasp on everything around him from then on. Gwen thinks he’s a bit off his rocker but tries to help him out nonetheless. Some of that is funny, not laugh out loud hilarious or anything, but it’s got a bit of a cute side to it all.<br /><br />Like many of KMM’s highlander romances, the heroine is beyond brilliant and the hero is nearly too gorgeous to look at. Problem with this: the heroine rarely acts smart even though she’s described as genius material, has a great job doing genius-like stuff but isn’t really all that invested in it and is always dissatisfied big time with her love life. They all want to find the great guy and have lots of babies right off the bat with them. Same holds true with Gwen. That’s all well and good but it turns into a cookie cutter formula romance by the third book in a series. As for Drustan he’s too beautiful for words and that got annoying because it’s repeated so many times. Sure he’s hot but he’s borderline boy toy sometimes because of his excessive hotness. It could’ve been toned down somewhat and more focus given on other things he could do. The love story between the two though is generally good and the steam is very hot but it drags in some parts –despite Drustan being a fabulous kisser, Moning highlighted that attribute quite well ;) Drustan’s Druidry and the Highland legends mix well to give a fairy-tale fantasy kind of world that’s continued from the first book. It was interesting but there was too much narration about it dragging the book down more often than not. <br /><br />There are a few side stories that start to develop between Drustan’s dad Sullivan and the housekeeper Nell as well as Drustran’s dark and mysterious brother Dageus. The main story though always remains the focus so these additional stories don’t detract from that and don’t feel like filler either. Both time periods are well represented and there are some funny moments with Gwen in his century and Drustan in hers.<br /><br />The ending is too sugary sweet for me but overall the story is alright so it just makes a 4 star rating. If you liked Circenn’s story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6138579.The_Highlander_s_Touch" title="The Highlander's Touch by K. Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">The Highlander's Touch</a> this one is about the same.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15760930200627864602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5sIzJJVkXc5njFsLsmsmIwidv8aodRpVEr5WwYyn+yoaWVi82rua15PN7lY0SFIB6tbEVDwaz664f+3sk0Y4Gw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xe6aEsElU6yGeMnybbvpEcTqDpOwoZ5j6XS+1scOLyU5dfGKjvqUtXI5fK/rmJ0zJqF1ASTOS5hDtQX72O/sFA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13103507137377857449">“The only other calling I ever felt was an irrepressible desire to be Captain of my own Starship. I was born in the wrong century and it wasn’t possible, so I chose to explore the universe by writing fiction instead. Books are doors to endless adventure.” -KMM<br/><br/>Karen Marie Moning is the #1 NYT bestselling author of the Fever Series and Highlander novels.<br/><br/>An alum of the Immaculate Conception Academy, </span>
  <span id="freeText13103507137377857449" style="display:none">“The only other calling I ever felt was an irrepressible desire to be Captain of my own Starship. I was born in the wrong century and it wasn’t possible, so I chose to explore the universe by writing fiction instead. Books are doors to endless adventure.” -KMM<br /><br />Karen Marie Moning is the #1 NYT bestselling author of the Fever Series and Highlander novels.<br /><br />An alum of the Immaculate Conception Academy, at seventeen she attended Purdue University where she completed a BA in Society &amp; Law, with minors in Philosophy, Creative Writing and Theatre, while working full time as a bartender and computer consultant. She intended to go to law school but after an internship with a firm of Criminal Attorneys, decided against it. For the next decade, she worked in insurance, where she wrote intercompany arbitrations and directed commercial litigation. At the age of thirty, she decided it was time to get serious and do what she’d always wanted to do: write fiction novels.<br /><br />Beyond the Highland Mist was published in 1999 and nominated for two RITA awards. She then published six more novels in her award-winning HIGHLANDER series, and received the RITA Award in 2001 for The Highlander’s Touch.<br /><br />In 2004, she began writing the #1 New York Times bestselling FEVER series. The books have been optioned twice for potential franchise development by Twentieth Century Fox and DreamWorks Studios, but the rights are currently held by Moning who has expressed a desire to one day see it as a television series. Her novels have been published in over thirty countries. She divides her time between Ohio and Florida and is working on two future projects for Random House Publishing.<br /><br />“I have always imagined that Paradise will be a kind of library.” – Jorge Luis Borges</span>
